  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2d36d38f-b160-43be-8a6d-e1189a5c1346'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1325548995" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1325548995?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1325548995" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13841149424848511523">Just as the limerick, “There once was a man from Nantucket –“ is the foulest yet most recognized of all, and just as the classic “Why did the chicken cross the road?” is the best joke, so is Robert A. Heinlein’s “All You Zombies-“ it is hands down the best time travel short story.<br/><br/>Published in 1960, a reader and fan can see the early ideas for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/353.Time_Enough_for_Love' title='Time Enough for Love by Robert A. Heinlein' rel='nofollow noopener'>Time Enough for Love</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/175325.I_Will_Fear_No_Evil' title='I Will Fear No Evil by Robert A. Heinlein' rel='nofollow noopener'>I Will Fear No Evil</a>. Was Heinlein a dirty old man? Yes, and in 1960, at the still young age of 53, he was just learning to fill ou</span>
  <span id="freeText13841149424848511523" style="display:none">Just as the limerick, “There once was a man from Nantucket –“ is the foulest yet most recognized of all, and just as the classic “Why did the chicken cross the road?” is the best joke, so is Robert A. Heinlein’s “All You Zombies-“ it is hands down the best time travel short story.<br><br>Published in 1960, a reader and fan can see the early ideas for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/353.Time_Enough_for_Love" title="Time Enough for Love by Robert A. Heinlein" rel="nofollow noopener">Time Enough for Love</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/175325.I_Will_Fear_No_Evil" title="I Will Fear No Evil by Robert A. Heinlein" rel="nofollow noopener">I Will Fear No Evil</a>. Was Heinlein a dirty old man? Yes, and in 1960, at the still young age of 53, he was just learning to fill out his garter and stockings.<br><br>I love the time travel section of the science fiction / fantasy genre. I love the weird ones, the quizzical ones and the ones you just can’t figure out. I love the good (H.G. Wells classic <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2493.The_Time_Machine" title="The Time Machine by H.G. Wells" rel="nofollow noopener">The Time Machine</a>), the bad (Piers Anthony’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/76659.Bearing_an_Hourglass__Incarnations_of_Immortality___2_" title="Bearing an Hourglass (Incarnations of Immortality, #2) by Piers Anthony" rel="nofollow noopener">Bearing An Hourglass</a>) and the ugly (Heinlein’s own Time Enough for Love). Poul Anderson’s many adventures in time needs special mention. <br><br>But for a short story to pack a lot into a small package, “All You Zombies-“ wins the prize.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517492856i/24981282.jpg" width="400" height="233" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="13841149424848511523" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8749020130235745358"><b>Never an Episode of Star Trek...</b><br/><br/>... And why not? Consciousness creates itself according to Heinlein. Forget about the mythical divine genesis stuff or that Darwinian evolution bunk. This is the real thing, the theory with oomph: time travel comes with the Homo sapiens territory, at least for the ones who can hack it (it’s the rest who are zombies).   <span id="freeText8749020130235745358" style="display:none"><b>Never an Episode of Star Trek...</b><br /><br />... And why not? Consciousness creates itself according to Heinlein. Forget about the mythical divine genesis stuff or that Darwinian evolution bunk. This is the real thing, the theory with oomph: time travel comes with the Homo sapiens territory, at least for the ones who can hack it (it’s the rest who are zombies). The perks are pretty spectacular - picking when and where you’re born for a start. And none of the neurotic consequences of family life. Literally no one to blame but yourself. Puts an entirely new perspective on the idea of solitary sex. Must have knocked their socks off in 1959. It’s still a bit of a whiz-bang. That’s probably why not.</span>

<div id="review_1325553401" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1325553401" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1325553401?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=dated-social-attitudes">dated-social-attitudes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1325553401" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1830534202189075172">A man walks into a bar. (Hah.) He gets into a conversation with the bartender, who wears a ring shaped like the worm Ouroboros. The barkeep is actually a "temporal agent." (What that means is revealed over the course of the story.)<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436050728i/15412706.jpg' width='300' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>The two men talk of many things: writing "true confession" stories, love lives, cads who love em' and leave em'... It turns out the guy at the bar is intersex (born with both sex organs, raised as a woman but now a man). Introduce time travel and a paradox or three an</span>
  <span id="freeText1830534202189075172" style="display:none">A man walks into a bar. (Hah.) He gets into a conversation with the bartender, who wears a ring shaped like the worm Ouroboros. The barkeep is actually a "temporal agent." (What that means is revealed over the course of the story.)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436050728i/15412706.jpg" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The two men talk of many things: writing "true confession" stories, love lives, cads who love em' and leave em'... It turns out the guy at the bar is intersex (born with both sex organs, raised as a woman but now a man). Introduce time travel and a paradox or three and you've got a short story guaranteed to make your brain whirl.<br><br>Heinlein was imaginative and brilliant but some of his viewpoints about free love, incest, etc., were pretty screwy. 1960, when this short story was written, is about the time Heinlein started really exploring these ideas in his fiction. Combine that with his outdated views about sexual stereotypes--in particular, in this story, astronauts are men, and any women who are interested in space can aspire to join the "Space Angels" group and become glorified hookers--and you've got a really weird backdrop to an otherwise intriguing exploration of time travel paradoxes.<br><br>You can read a copy of this story online <a href="http://cla.calpoly.edu/~lcall/303/heinlein_all_you_zombies.pdf" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1830534202189075172" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer570495578" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17715109625978055971">Re-read 6/2/18:<br/><br/>Nostalgia hits again. :) Thinking about doing a lot more Heinlein reads fairly soon. :)<br/><br/>Original Review:<br/><br/>I had to reread this after just watching Predestination on which it was based. I was impressed with the movie but even more so with the story. I guess I picked up more nuances this time. It was all the more impressive because of how the character study really played out and what wasn't said but could be deduced. I think I can thank the movie more for that aspect, although one sto</span>
  <span id="freeText17715109625978055971" style="display:none">Re-read 6/2/18:<br /><br />Nostalgia hits again. :) Thinking about doing a lot more Heinlein reads fairly soon. :)<br /><br />Original Review:<br /><br />I had to reread this after just watching Predestination on which it was based. I was impressed with the movie but even more so with the story. I guess I picked up more nuances this time. It was all the more impressive because of how the character study really played out and what wasn't said but could be deduced. I think I can thank the movie more for that aspect, although one storyline hadn't existed in the short story.<br /><br />Even so, very impressive ideas and a minimalist style that was so understated that I'm not too surprised I missed it the first time. Preferred some of his other short stories more, but maybe I need to revisit them all and see how my grown-up-self takes them. <br /><br />What can I say? It was tight and impactive and so very easy to see how it informed the later third of his novels in both strangeness and, dare I say it, incestuousness? Absolutely, but I'm of a mind that Heinlein is still the Grandmaster and should retain the title forever, regardless of the kinds of stunts he has been known to play. After all, he's not merely informative and didactic. He's one hell of a storyteller.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17715109625978055971" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1283970134022728866">Next up on my Book then Movie list was this 1950’s short story that was later adapted into Predestination in 2014.<br/><br/>This Sci-Fi time travelling paradox was so bizarre that even at its modest page count really makes an impact.<br/>It’s the type of story that I really enjoy!<br/><br/>The story starts with a young man walking into a bar and strikes up a conversation with the time-traveling bartender. <br/>The reader soon learns how the two are connected and the significance of snake-swallowing-his-tail ring on the barke</span>
  <span id="freeText1283970134022728866" style="display:none">Next up on my Book then Movie list was this 1950’s short story that was later adapted into Predestination in 2014.<br /><br />This Sci-Fi time travelling paradox was so bizarre that even at its modest page count really makes an impact.<br />It’s the type of story that I really enjoy!<br /><br />The story starts with a young man walking into a bar and strikes up a conversation with the time-traveling bartender. <br />The reader soon learns how the two are connected and the significance of snake-swallowing-his-tail ring on the barkeep's finger.<br /><br />I’m sure this story is going to leave a lasting impression on me, I find the best movie adaptations are based on short stories as there’s room to expand the narrative.<br />It’s a really quick half hour read, excited to watch the movie now!</span>

<div id="review_1011271133" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1011271133" />
    <a title="Althea Ann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3846743-althea-ann"><img alt="Althea Ann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411566466p2/3846743.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1011271133?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Althea Ann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Althea Ann" href="/user/show/3846743-althea-ann">Althea Ann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1011271133" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10332557716886167578">This is a time paradox story. It's not specifically *about* gender, but Heinlein's deeply sexist assumptions about how gender affects personality and his assumptions about how even a future society's sexism will not change in any way, are fully on display here. (In the future, women don't become 'spacemen,' they are sent to be 'comfort women' for lonely spacemen who can't control their 'urges.' The possibility of a woman being a competent astronaut isn't even considered.) <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Unless, </span></span>
  <span id="freeText10332557716886167578" style="display:none">This is a time paradox story. It's not specifically *about* gender, but Heinlein's deeply sexist assumptions about how gender affects personality and his assumptions about how even a future society's sexism will not change in any way, are fully on display here. (In the future, women don't become 'spacemen,' they are sent to be 'comfort women' for lonely spacemen who can't control their 'urges.' The possibility of a woman being a competent astronaut isn't even considered.) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Unless, of course, she actually becomes a man. Apparently male hormones confer said competence. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Ugh.<br />I didn't find the ramifications of the time-travel dilemma, as presented here, as interesting or 'mind-blowing' as other readers have.<br /><br />PS, there are no zombies in this story. (not that the fact makes it a better or worse story, but if you're a zombie fiction completist, it's just something to be aware of...)<br /><br />[Just a note: I read this story directly after reading an editor's note complaining that Heinlein's writing is often dismissed due to its supposed misogyny (a charge, he implied, which is untrue and unfair) - so that probably caused me to be more alert to the topic that I might've been otherwise.] </span>
  <a data-text-id="10332557716886167578" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17238487-all-you-zombies">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2410669403" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12022454506905697378">Wow. Just ... wow.<br/><br/>A man walks into a bar ... in this case that is NOT a joke. *lol*<br/>The man is a writer and was born female. He has frequented the bar for the past few years but only now is talking to the bartender, telling his/her story of getting pregnant and ending up then and there.<br/>The rest is a very surprising, mind-boggling time travel story full of paradoxes that makes perfect sense.<br/><br/>According to my research, Heinlein wrote this story in one afternoon. It's amazing if one considers all the </span>
  <span id="freeText12022454506905697378" style="display:none">Wow. Just ... wow.<br /><br />A man walks into a bar ... in this case that is NOT a joke. *lol*<br />The man is a writer and was born female. He has frequented the bar for the past few years but only now is talking to the bartender, telling his/her story of getting pregnant and ending up then and there.<br />The rest is a very surprising, mind-boggling time travel story full of paradoxes that makes perfect sense.<br /><br />According to my research, Heinlein wrote this story in one afternoon. It's amazing if one considers all the subjects he's touching upon and how intricate the plot is.<br /><br />I must say that due to his view on women, I'm not much of a fan. This view is portrayed in this story as well by the "Space Angels" (basically hookers for astronauts). And no, the time he lived in cannot always simply explain or excuse it away.<br />However, he seems to have been a gifted author with intelligent stories to tell (sometimes at least) and this one was truly brilliantly executed. Though I did know where he would take the story thanks to the bartender mentioning his ring, it was awesome to be taken on that journey.<br /><br />But only read this if your mind is primed for timey-wimey stuff. ;)</span>
  <a data-text-id="12022454506905697378" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1405080566" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1405080566" />
    <a title="Annie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24476089-annie"><img alt="Annie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1503503332p2/24476089.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1405080566?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie" href="/user/show/24476089-annie">Annie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">It's fewer than ten pages goddammit. Read it! </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24476089-annie?shelf=sf">sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24476089-annie?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24476089-annie?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1405080566" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5621645349240890853"><br/><p>Heinlein presents one of the most mind boggling paradoxes presented by, or rather resulted from, time travel. All time travel stories are complicated, they survive on a merry go round of events and a dramatic sequence of effect and consequence. But in “All You Zombies”, Heinlein goes a step farther and designs a story line of an infinite loop, where the interchange of cause and effect lands the reader into a ‘chicken and egg’ situation. </p><br/><p>You ask who came first. Thematically the story says what do</p></span>
  <span id="freeText5621645349240890853" style="display:none"><br /><p>Heinlein presents one of the most mind boggling paradoxes presented by, or rather resulted from, time travel. All time travel stories are complicated, they survive on a merry go round of events and a dramatic sequence of effect and consequence. But in “All You Zombies”, Heinlein goes a step farther and designs a story line of an infinite loop, where the interchange of cause and effect lands the reader into a ‘chicken and egg’ situation. </p><br /><p>You ask who came first. Thematically the story says what does it matter? Yes, it is a time travel story. And the sheer imaginative droppings of that part are brilliant in itself. But the story also illustrates a pretty heavy picture of the alienation that surrounds individuals who not conform. The protagonist is introduced in the story with the name ‘Unmarried Mother’ and he is a man who writes confession columns. That idea evokes hilarity towards a lonely and evidently bitter man who makes a living by pretending to be women, but at the same time the name ‘Unmarried Mother’ throws a shade on the darkness of the individual. As the story delves deeper, and we as readers are acquainted more and more closely with the character, this segregation, this alienation and prejudice becomes more and more apparent.</p><br /><p>Heinlein closes the story with an open ending, although there was really no way around it, what with the story resembling the snake that eats its own tail. And the closing is a cry, a wail for the things lost, for the time that is lost. </p><br /><p>The paradox contained in this short marvel isn’t just limited to temporal shift, but is also contained in the name of the story. In the end, too. Heinlein declares the world in the story and broadly us, the readers to be Zombies i.e., mindless creatures. Therein lies the question that be true, what was the purpose of the protagonist who attempts to save lives via time travel? Is saving souls that are doomed, glorifying the saver or is just, for once, conforming him to crowd and acting the saviour?</p><br /><p>This is a dark story and I am told it is in the same vein as “By His Bootstraps’, although I am yet to read that, but it is one of the best of what I have read. I have been reading a lot of short stories lately, and I am amazed at the punch a few pages can pack. And as far as “All You Zombies” is concerned, don’t be daunted by its size! ;)</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="5621645349240890853" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2934919082885602217"><i>Never Do Yesterday What Should Be Done Tomorrow.<br/>If at Last You Do Succeed, Never Try Again.<br/>A Stitch in Time Saves Nine Billion.<br/>A Paradox May Be Paradoctored.<br/>It Is Earlier When You Think.<br/>Ancestors Are Just People.<br/>Even Jove Nods.</i><br/><br/><br/>A long time ago I've seen a movie called <i>Predestination</i>, but just recently I've found out that it was adopted from a short story called <i>All You Zombies</i>, so of course I had to read it. And just like the movie blew my mind, so did this story. The movie did add a lot of amazi</span>
  <span id="freeText2934919082885602217" style="display:none"><i>Never Do Yesterday What Should Be Done Tomorrow.<br />If at Last You Do Succeed, Never Try Again.<br />A Stitch in Time Saves Nine Billion.<br />A Paradox May Be Paradoctored.<br />It Is Earlier When You Think.<br />Ancestors Are Just People.<br />Even Jove Nods.</i><br /><br /><br />A long time ago I've seen a movie called <i>Predestination</i>, but just recently I've found out that it was adopted from a short story called <i>All You Zombies</i>, so of course I had to read it. And just like the movie blew my mind, so did this story. The movie did add a lot of amazing twists and turns, but for some reason I enjoyed this short story a bit more. It was quite simple, but mind-blowing at the same time. And I would definitely recommend it to anyone who likes to read short amazing stories, with a lot of twists thrown in.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8806254973100233679">Wow. In the middle of the book I realized that the story is oddly familiar. Then I remembered that I have seen the film with the likewise story: Predestination, which I really loved. The story left me speechless. It is a complex time-travel gender paradox story, asking the question of : what would happen if you go back in time and marry yourself? Damn, it is fascinating.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1403031993" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1403031993" />
    <a title="Owlseyes " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6132231-owlseyes"><img alt="Owlseyes " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594656251p2/6132231.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1403031993?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Owlseyes " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Owlseyes " href="/user/show/6132231-owlseyes">Owlseyes </a>
      </span>

          marked it as to-read




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6132231-owlseyes?shelf=us-lit">us-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6132231-owlseyes?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6132231-owlseyes?shelf=time-travel-paradox">time-travel-paradox</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1403031993" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4253054891337349751"><b>Time travel can be disorienting.<br/>Very true.</b><br/><br/><a href='http://imgur.com/1dnwxC4' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443461507i/16362969._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Some time ago I have watched the movie “Predestination” by Michael Spierig, based on the story written by Heinlein.<br/><br/>The characters' structure is, apparently, simple. <br/><br/>In a bar, traumatized male A meets male B. <br/><br/>While talking, B reveals he was a female once, but her ovaries and uterus had been removed and the name has been changed. <br/><br/>B is also traumatized because she’d known a man ( let’s call him B´), and they had a child. …never to be seen again,… after </span>
  <span id="freeText4253054891337349751" style="display:none"><b>Time travel can be disorienting.<br>Very true.</b><br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/1dnwxC4" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443461507i/16362969._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Some time ago I have watched the movie “Predestination” by Michael Spierig, based on the story written by Heinlein.<br><br>The characters' structure is, apparently, simple. <br><br>In a bar, traumatized male A meets male B. <br><br>While talking, B reveals he was a female once, but her ovaries and uterus had been removed and the name has been changed. <br><br>B is also traumatized because she’d known a man ( let’s call him B´), and they had a child. …never to be seen again,… after birth. The baby was kidnapped, and the father (B') just disappeared. <br><br>Subject A thinks he can help subject B, because he’s able to travel back in time and sort things out, so to speak. So they both travel back in time. <br><br>Subject B finds out that the girl he met is none other but himself….when female.<br><br> [!]<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/tRvv23r" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443461507i/16362970._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Even for A things get complicated; while trying to fix his own trauma, he meets his (sort of) nemesis; let’s call him A’, the one who caused A’s trauma. <br><br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/zfNKRqL" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443461507i/16362971.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>While arguing, A concludes they’re not “mergeable” (as B and B’ did, in fact); so A kills A´ saying: “I’ll never become you”. <br><br><br>…it’s a “predestination paradox”, you may wonder about the rest. Let’s just say that A was the one who kidnapped the baby child.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4253054891337349751" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1064841135" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1064841135" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6751264-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319310056p2/6751264.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1064841135?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/6751264-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17238487-all-you-zombies">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6751264-becky?shelf=short-stories-essays">short-stories-essays</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1064841135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2727907985524039625">I recently came across a trailer for a new movie from the Spierig brothers and decided to seek out the source story - to aid in my attempt to read more sci-fi in general and more classic sci-fi in particular. The movie is called Predestination and stars Ethan Hawke as "the Bartender" a time traveling cop. It played at this year's South by Southwest and apparently did really well. Well enough, in fact, to get picked up for distribution. <br/><br/>A quick look-see at the movie's dets shows that it is in fac</span>
  <span id="freeText2727907985524039625" style="display:none">I recently came across a trailer for a new movie from the Spierig brothers and decided to seek out the source story - to aid in my attempt to read more sci-fi in general and more classic sci-fi in particular. The movie is called Predestination and stars Ethan Hawke as "the Bartender" a time traveling cop. It played at this year's South by Southwest and apparently did really well. Well enough, in fact, to get picked up for distribution. <br /><br />A quick look-see at the movie's dets shows that it is in fact based on a short story penned by Robert A. Heinlein and published back in 1959 (if Wikipedia is to be trusted) in Fantasy and Science Fiction magazine. BTW, don't read the actual Wikipedia breakdown of the story if you want the story or movie to be any sort of surprise.<br /><br />"All You Zombies" is weird and cool and super bizarre. It's also extremely short. Supposedly, though, the Spierig brothers have stuck close to their inspiration while also fleshing out and obviously adding more of an investigation plot. <br /><br />In the short, the Bartender is set on recruiting a character called the Unmarried Mother. The Unmarried Mother has a troubled past that is revealed to the Bartender during their talk - over drinks - with the Bartender ultimately suggesting he can help the Unmarried Mother in gaining some vengeance or closure. In exchange, the Unmarried Mother will sign on as a fellow temporal agent. <br /><br />It's hard to say much about the story without completely ruining it, and I do feel a bit of a sense of regret in now knowing at least part of the movie plot as well. I'm sure there's lots that can be debated about the story, but all in all it's a time travel paradox story. Everything in the story hinges on specific events that must happen via time travel. <br /><br />I'm not sure how I really want to rate this read. On the one hand I know it's a classic of the genre and Heinlein is a HUGE name in said genre as well. On the other hand it's just such a weird story! It might require another read through before seeing the film.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2727907985524039625" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1413110314" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14039387381081250147">Time travel theory and its paradoxes always elude me and traveling across time (I don't want to go into the future, I can imagine how it will be like/ends, I'm fascinated by the past, I'm inquisitive) remains a curious idea.<br/><br/>It all started with the Bar scene, a reluctant conversation between a man and the bartender, soon turns into an interesting one, then emotional and finally breaks into next level. <br/><br/>First twist of the story, I was like <i>Okay! I am catching up </i>, my expectations were very high (I </span>
  <span id="freeText14039387381081250147" style="display:none">Time travel theory and its paradoxes always elude me and traveling across time (I don't want to go into the future, I can imagine how it will be like/ends, I'm fascinated by the past, I'm inquisitive) remains a curious idea.<br /><br />It all started with the Bar scene, a reluctant conversation between a man and the bartender, soon turns into an interesting one, then emotional and finally breaks into next level. <br /><br />First twist of the story, I was like <i>Okay! I am catching up </i>, my expectations were very high (I heard a lot about its movie adaptation <i>Predestination </i> in my film circles by then), and it served brilliantly. Story was just unfolding, we were shifting timelines, time zones and fates as well, all blended intelligently.<br /><br />But after the final twist<br /><br /><i>You know who she is, and you understand who you are, and now maybe you are ready to understand who I am.</i><br /><br />I was like lost, completely, I submitted myself to the beauty of this story. Then, the obvious, asking questions, seeking answers, changing equations, satisfied smiles and so on. Clearly I was fooled by the book's size.<br /><br />A personal thought: Movie adaptation was better though. Recommended.</span>

<div id="review_382919353" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/382919353" />
    <a title="Jacob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/901342-jacob"><img alt="Jacob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555491633p2/901342.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/382919353?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacob" href="/user/show/901342-jacob">Jacob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/901342-jacob?shelf=science_fiction">science_fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/901342-jacob?shelf=from_library">from_library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer382919353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12576795717045777874">Although this Heinlein story probably isn't for everyone, it IS an interesting exercise in figuring out how someone could be their own father _and_ mother through the mechanism of time travel. What makes this good to read is the writing; in a time travel story you have more flexibility in the order you write the scenes, and Heinlein's arrangement keeps the suspense while effectively doling out the story in an order one can keep up with and understand. I've read this one before (last year, I thin</span>
  <span id="freeText12576795717045777874" style="display:none">Although this Heinlein story probably isn't for everyone, it IS an interesting exercise in figuring out how someone could be their own father _and_ mother through the mechanism of time travel. What makes this good to read is the writing; in a time travel story you have more flexibility in the order you write the scenes, and Heinlein's arrangement keeps the suspense while effectively doling out the story in an order one can keep up with and understand. I've read this one before (last year, I think), and it actually rewards rereading with a lot of foreshadow at the front that one can recognize and appreciate better the second time.<br /><br />I wanted to read this because of the title, which is shared with a song I like by The Hooters. The funny thing is that I still haven't figured out why the story is titled this way and why the main character says it at the end. It makes so little sense to me that I didn't realize I'd already read this story until I started reading it (again), because the title has no association with the story for me. Still doesn't.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12576795717045777874" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1632096385" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer6954492888556923003">"Ever hear the expression 'A ruined Woman'?<br/>"Mmm, years ago, Doesn't mean much today."<br/>"I am as ruined as a woman can be; .... "<br/><br/>So, much depth in these three lines , completely change the story!<br/>If you thought Inception was 'mindfuck' , I think this book/ short story gives it a tough competition.<br/>The movie adaptation of this book 'Predestination' is one of those movies which actually do justice to the original! The movie is an extended version of this book and is way better!<br/><br/>But, the book is one of t</span>
  <span id="freeText6954492888556923003" style="display:none">"Ever hear the expression 'A ruined Woman'?<br />"Mmm, years ago, Doesn't mean much today."<br />"I am as ruined as a woman can be; .... "<br /><br />So, much depth in these three lines , completely change the story!<br />If you thought Inception was 'mindfuck' , I think this book/ short story gives it a tough competition.<br />The movie adaptation of this book 'Predestination' is one of those movies which actually do justice to the original! The movie is an extended version of this book and is way better!<br /><br />But, the book is one of the best time-travel paradox based story I've ever read!<br /><br />A fifteen minute read, that'll leave you in a whole different world for a few days!<br />A must read!</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tgL9Rc/qXWfUNQOYEuUF5/ZHf4LxzTg6L9pK+qxroWaX0TY/SCtoQYik8b9xZAlW8uwlklFvvt5dPqLLvaZiWA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZtUyIgpssgDQmtUDyLJ4ucXVur2949esxnp0mhpR0yRHBvlYja2HJowLJySrM3QIwX7grR1BUUi0npyrC5wQGg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16373561490961058962">Robert Anson Heinlein was an American novelist and science fiction writer. Often called "the dean of science fiction writers", he is one of the most popular, influential, and controversial authors of "hard science fiction". <br/><br/>He set a high standard for science and engineering plausibility and helped to raise the genre's standards of literary quality. He was the first SF writer to break into mainstre</span>
  <span id="freeText16373561490961058962" style="display:none">Robert Anson Heinlein was an American novelist and science fiction writer. Often called "the dean of science fiction writers", he is one of the most popular, influential, and controversial authors of "hard science fiction". <br /><br />He set a high standard for science and engineering plausibility and helped to raise the genre's standards of literary quality. He was the first SF writer to break into mainstream, general magazines such as <i>The Saturday Evening Post</i>, in the late 1940s. He was also among the first authors of bestselling, novel-length science fiction in the modern, mass-market era. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16373561490961058962" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
